<span id="freeTextContainer2187773554917709947"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521068603i/25214763.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>Human: </b>Did you hear that? <br/><b>Me: </b>Yeah, that was just the sound of my expectations shattering on the concrete after jumping from the tenth floor. <br/><br/><b>*Sighs* </b><br/><br/>Where do I even start? <br/><br/>Somebody please explain the hype to me because I honestly don’t get it. Usually when I dislike a popular book, I can at least see why other people might enjoy it. This time however, I do not see it. <br/><br/>Okay! Before anyone bites my head off, let me just explain everything I disliked about the book. <br/><br/><b>The writing style </b><br/><br/><i>"Rowan let o</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2187773554917709947" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521068603i/25214763.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Human: </b>Did you hear that? <br><b>Me: </b>Yeah, that was just the sound of my expectations shattering on the concrete after jumping from the tenth floor. <br><br><b>*Sighs* </b><br><br>Where do I even start? <br><br>Somebody please explain the hype to me because I honestly don’t get it. Usually when I dislike a popular book, I can at least see why other people might enjoy it. This time however, I do not see it. <br><br>Okay! Before anyone bites my head off, let me just explain everything I disliked about the book. <br><br><b>The writing style </b><br><br><i>"Rowan let out his breath, not even realizing he had been holding it." </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521068603ra/25214764.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><s>Somebody glean me before I glean myself. </s><br><br>➨Why is this sentence still a thing? Why is it still legal to use? I thought the human race had moved on from this. I thought we were making progress! <b>*Lets out a breath she perfectly knew she had been holding*</b><br><br>If it wasn’t for the hype, I would have DNFed it right after reading that sentence. You just can’t expect anything good to come out of a book that has the holding breath sentence, that’s just not possible. I should have known better. <br><br>➨There’s also something about the head-hopping/ omniscient narration(?) that just rubbed me the wrong way. We kept randomly jumping from one character’s head to the next and this might be just a personal preference thing, but I did not enjoy it at all. <br><br><b>The Romance </b><br>➨It’s been a while since I read a romance that felt this cringy. To be fair, it takes a lot for me to like the romance in any book. What can I say, I have high standards when it comes to romance (blame Colleen Hoover). <b>But, </b> I can tell you this isn’t me being picky about my ships. The romance in this book felt extremely forced, insta-lovey and just weird at times. I basically skimmed most of the second half of the book, but I swear there was something in there about her licking his blood. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520549884ra/25183833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br> <b>The Plot</b><br>➨Even though this book is essentially about murdering people, it’s surprisingly uneventful. I found myself bored out of my mind for a good chunk of the book and that’s just something I never expected based on the premise. <br><br>➨The amount of plot holes in this book is just concerning. There were a lot of things that didn’t add up and so many ‘rules’ of the world that were just ignored whenever convenient. <b>UGH. </b><br><br>➨Also, every single “plot twist” in this book can be seen from two miles away. Without glasses. In the dark. Just sayin’.<br><br>Overall, Scythe was not for me. If you’ve enjoyed this book, please let me know in the comments what aspects of it you liked. I would genuinely love to know. <br><br>Thanks for reading! Please share your thoughts. <br><br>-----------------------------------------------<br><b>Pre-reading </b><br>I remember loving Unwind by Neal Shusterman so I'm very excited to dive into his newer series. I've heard great things about it so let's see how I feel about it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450520360ra/17439087.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2187773554917709947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1593860557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593860557" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593860557?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593860557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6064364594760059253"><b>So this book is basically just about murder. Exciting!</b> All I want to do is say "MURDER, JOHN" like Sherlock wood, so imagine me doing that. Anyway! I had super high expectations for this because every blogger, bookworm, and semi-literate fish I know has <i>raved</i> over it. I also love <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep' title='Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Challenger Deep</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764347.Unwind__Unwind___1_' title='Unwind (Unwind, #1) by Neal Shusterman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unwind</a> a LOT, so I knew this was going to be excellent!<br/><br/><b>+ It's a dystopian with this perfect world where there is no death: so some people become scythes to keep the balance.</b><br/>This is a very cool premis</span>
  <span id="freeText6064364594760059253" style="display:none"><b>So this book is basically just about murder. Exciting!</b> All I want to do is say "MURDER, JOHN" like Sherlock wood, so imagine me doing that. Anyway! I had super high expectations for this because every blogger, bookworm, and semi-literate fish I know has <i>raved</i> over it. I also love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Challenger Deep</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764347.Unwind__Unwind___1_" title="Unwind (Unwind, #1) by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Unwind</a> a LOT, so I knew this was going to be excellent!<br /><br /><b>+ It's a dystopian with this perfect world where there is no death: so some people become scythes to keep the balance.</b><br />This is a very cool premise althoooough, we have this like "perfect world" but the scythes could be pretty gruesome and cruel with their gleaning tactics. (Knives? Flamethrowers? Guns?? Etc??) That <i>did not make sense to me</i>. I feel like the scythes should've gleaned in a more anti-harm way to keep that vibe of "humanity is perfect and has reached levels of perfection". Anyhow.<br /><br /><b>+ The scythes had freaking awesome robes and I want one.</b><br />I mean. Look at that cover. I NEED A ROBE LIKE THAT.<br /><br /><b>+ I really liked both Citra and Rowan!</b><br />The story is split between them and as they're apprenticed to Scythe Faraday (although reluctantly) and they're both kind of winning. Citra is a bit of a Slytherin go-getter and Rowan is a self confessed "lettuce" (aka: unimportant and forgettable) (which I'm really pleased he used that term because I've bene using it FOREVER HA!). I didn't exactly connect to either of them though?! The narration felt a bit distant (which is unusual; I generally adore 3rd person), but I still was SUPER keen to see how their story would unfold. <b>I really loved their relationship too!!</b> (And honestly if you're into books with very very <i>very</i> little romance: This is for you.)<br /><br />ALSO THE BOOK IS VERY MEAN TO ROWAN AND MY POOR HEART.❤️💔<br /><br /><b>+ It is kind of long though?!</b><br />I felt it was a teeny tiny bit rambly, and it took me a while to get invested because there wasn't much plot but Citra and Rowan training to be scythes. But at the same time it was ENJOYABLE TO READ!! I just wasn't mind-smackingly (is that a word??? it is now) invested.<br /><br /><b>+ AND THEN THE TWISTS CAME.</b><br />Like hit me in the face with a brick, why don't you. One of the twists had me kind of going "OH. I DIDN'T WANT THAT" which is a masterfully great feeling. Who needs happiness! Not bookworms!<br /><br /><b>+ Also the world building was fab.</b><br />It reminded me of the Giver nearly!? But they all had technology to make them reset their ages and everyone lived in comfort, but still had to work and strive etc. And the details of the world just really made it so easy to get lost in. I am also totally down with this being our future if everytime you potential die you get revived and given ice cream. Dessert cures!! I've said this my whole life!!<br /><br /><b>So definitely glad I (finally) read this one! Yes I am late to the scythedom highway to hell but happy to be here, fren.</b> It wasn't the world's most "perfect" read for me, and I'm a little disappointed I didn't love it 100%. But I wANT THE NEXT ONE. And I'd recommend it in a heartbeat, especially if you give me ice cream. There is death, corruption, feels and knives. Yes please and thank you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6064364594760059253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12150996481085287332" style="display:none"><blockquote><b> A world where natural death is obsolete thereby requiring a dedicated use of "Sycthes" (who are the only ones authorised to kill) and while most Scythes honour the process, there are a few bad apples who use their powers for evil. </b><br /><br />And so the killing ensues.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2325306262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2325306262" />
    <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara"><img alt="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537347712p2/43416866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2325306262?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara">Evgnossia O&#39;Hara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2325306262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2763643035443558124">See this review on my BookTube channel <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YhH_h9PMfrY&lc=Ugy9ObBoeCMsC72GPQp4AaABAg' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>. It's in Greek but, I plan a lot of interesting things in English as well :)<br/><br/>Review was originally published on my Blog <a href='https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2018/05/29/scythe-by-neal-shusterman-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through the Chapters</a><br/><br/>I’m in minority given the high ratings and the positives reviews on this book, but I want to be honest regarding my reading experience and the truth is that I <b>struggled reading</b> Shythe. The premise was interesting, but it was the only interesting part of the story. You might as well read the synopsis and mark the boo</span>
  <span id="freeText2763643035443558124" style="display:none">See this review on my BookTube channel <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YhH_h9PMfrY&amp;lc=Ugy9ObBoeCMsC72GPQp4AaABAg" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. It's in Greek but, I plan a lot of interesting things in English as well :)<br><br>Review was originally published on my Blog <a href="https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2018/05/29/scythe-by-neal-shusterman-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Chapters</a><br><br>I’m in minority given the high ratings and the positives reviews on this book, but I want to be honest regarding my reading experience and the truth is that I <b>struggled reading</b> Shythe. The premise was interesting, but it was the only interesting part of the story. You might as well read the synopsis and mark the book as “read”.<br><br>So, it is a story about a utopian community where people have conquered hunger, disease, war, misery and even death. The only way to control the increase of population is by having people, also known as Shythes, to kill other people. Citra and Rowan are chosen to apprentice to a scythe. Basically, the whole book – 435 pages – is about their apprenticeship and a controversial love story.<br><br>The <b>Shythes</b> are divided into two categories. The <b>empathetic ones</b>, who glean (a term they used instead of murder) because they have to; quickly, <b>painless</b>, demonstrating their soft-hearts for sobbing after the execution of their victims. After the “mandatory” duty, they attend the funerals to show off their superiority and to remind humanity, that this is the way the things work. And thus, implying their “unwillingness” to act in these patterns and stressing their roles as means, since they care about the greater good of the society – the freaking <b>hypocrites</b>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>“It is the most difficult thing a person can be asked to do. And knowing that it is for the greater good doesn’t make it any easier.”</i>
  </p>
</blockquote> ⇒ <u>Hypocrites</u> <br><br><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>“Will the scythe who replaces me be as compassionate and fair?”</i>
  </p>
</blockquote> ⇒ <u>Is it possible to be compassionate and fair when it comes to the deprivation of human life?</u> <br><br>The second category consists of the <b>evils</b>, <b>the serial killers</b>, <b>the psychopaths</b>, who usually are involved in massacres (Jesus freaking Christ). Oh, did I mention that they have a “system” to choose the next victim? A lame “system”, which can somehow excuse the fact they are <b>cold-blooded killers</b> and not the angels of death, who were chosen to maintain the stability. However, the reality is much simpler. They were chosen to kill, just to spice up the peaceful existence in the utopian world they existed. I see them as assassins, who had been selected by a perverted “government”, <u>to keep the people under control and fear</u>. To feel their unlimited power and to enjoy the act of killing other people, because they just could, without any impact.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527580952ra/25613405.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What about the <b>romance</b>? Sorry, was there any romance? The main characters were indifferent to me. I won’t even refer to that kiss. The confession of their feelings seemed <b>rushed</b> and <b>forced</b> to me. How did they fall in love since there wasn’t even a platonic chemistry between them? Sorry, but it is not enough for me when it comes to romance.<br><br>One of the reasons I picked this book up was the expectation of some really awesome <b>plot twists</b>. Yes, I agree that my mind was blown due to the amount of cliché twists I witnessed. I saw them coming from a mile away, given the fact I’m myopic.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527580952ra/25613404.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally, I want to point out the <b>frustrating behaviour</b> of the ordinary people, who consider “Shythes” as celebrities. They <b>admire</b> them, they meet them with <b>applauds</b> on the “red carpet”. The “ordinary”, immortal humans entertain themselves by <b>watching indifferently</b> the blood bath the murderers create. The utopia they are living in made them <b>heartless</b>, <b>apathetic</b> towards their fellow beings, as soon as they have their immunity, and therefore safety for a year or so. They have transformed into a crooked community, which is trying to gain the patronage of the shythes by bribing and serving them. The aforementioned are painfully familiar and the most intimidating part of the story, since it <u>describes perfectly the real world</u>. They (we) know, they (we) understand, and still they (we) do it.<br><br>Thanks for reading and I hope that you won’t glean me due to my extremely negative review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2763643035443558124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1632025895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632025895" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632025895?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29246020-scythe">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Unwind, Black Mirrors</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632025895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10048581112013599827"><b>Kindle Daily Deal 20Oct19 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Scythe-Arc-Book-1-ebook/dp/B01BKR487W/ref=lp_6165851011_1_8?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1571585376&sr=1-8' rel='nofollow noopener'>$4.95</a></b> This was one of my favorite reads of 2016. <br/><br/>Reread with some BB&Bers<br/><br/><a href='http://imgur.com/FBRSvM9' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480973982i/21370455._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>What if</b> you could kill people and be Death himself.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480974058i/21370461.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>What if</b> cancer and all the worlds diseases were healed and our understanding of how to heal everybody was so great that you could pretty much save anyone from practically anything that would have killed them. <br/><br/><b>What if</b> you could totally turn back the clock so that even though you are fifty-two or seventy-five you could look like you were in your </span>
  <span id="freeText10048581112013599827" style="display:none"><b>Kindle Daily Deal 20Oct19 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Scythe-Arc-Book-1-ebook/dp/B01BKR487W/ref=lp_6165851011_1_8?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1571585376&amp;sr=1-8" rel="nofollow noopener">$4.95</a></b> This was one of my favorite reads of 2016. <br><br>Reread with some BB&amp;Bers<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/FBRSvM9" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480973982i/21370455._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>What if</b> you could kill people and be Death himself.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480974058i/21370461.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What if</b> cancer and all the worlds diseases were healed and our understanding of how to heal everybody was so great that you could pretty much save anyone from practically anything that would have killed them. <br><br><b>What if</b> you could totally turn back the clock so that even though you are fifty-two or seventy-five you could look like you were in your twenties.<br><br><b>What if</b> there was nothing like war, poverty or hunger because artificial intelligence wasn’t a bad thing and it was better at running the world than the politicians and warmongers.<br><blockquote>
  <i> The greatest achievement of the human race was not conquering death. It was ending government. Back in the days when the world’s digital network was called “the cloud,” people thought giving too much power to an artificial intelligence would be a very bad idea. Cautionary tales abounded in every form of media. The machines were always the enemy. But then the cloud evolved into the Thunderhead, sparking with consciousness, or at least a remarkable facsimile. In stark contrast to people’s fears, the Thunderhead did not seize power. Instead, it was people who came to realize that it was far better suited to run things than politicians.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>What if</b> selected humans were now charged with culling the population and causing the deaths of those chosen. That they themselves had to choose who to kill and perform the execution becoming walking death.<br><br><b>What if</b> you were chosen to be apprenticed to one of these people and learn how to kill.<br><br><b>What if……</b> well you get the gist.<br><br>I used to read a lot of YA but after a while so much of it seemed the same. After the fifteenth time in the book someone released a breath they didn’t know they were holding or dollface’s eyes became darker (<i>cuz that is what happens when you lust after someone</i>) and she threw away everything special about herself for Jerkwad A I was over it. <b>But then I found Neal Shusterman (NS).</b> I think that NS is the king of what if…. He takes something from our society today and tweaks it extremely to the best/worst case scenario and TaH-DaH magic.<br><br>Neal Shusterman has been on my autobuy list since I read his Unwind series which is my favorite completely YA and Dystopian series to date. While this is completely different in the world and the characters one thing remains the same. This book is for people who like to ponder the “what ifs” of the world and society. Like….<br><blockquote>
  <i> To date, the oldest living human being is somewhere around three hundred, but only because we are still so close to the Age of Mortality. I wonder what life will be like a millennium from now, when the average age will be nearer to one thousand. Will we all be renaissance children, skilled at every art and science, because we’ve had the time to master them? Or will boredom and slavish routine plague us even more than it does today, giving us less of a reason to live limitless lives? I dream of the former, but suspect the latter.</i>
</blockquote><br>This story follows Rowan and Cirta as they start their internship of a year with Sythe Faraday learning everything there is to know about what it takes to be a killer of men. Which is less about learning how to kill, although there is some of that, and more about finding a path they can live with. Watching people die isn’t as easy as one would think. There are moral quandaries and it seems that not all the Scythes believe in the same things. Could it be in this society where a fraction of the people die compared to the Age of Mortality that there are things going on in the politics of death that might lead to disaster???<br><br>As the story delves into the deeper politics of death and how the world might be changing I liked seeing how a few of the different Scythes treated the responsibility of killing and how each seemed to have a different process and a different way to deal with families and after affects. People are people and it seems that if you give some of them enough power corruption is bound to bleed through.<br><br>There is a very small aspect of romance between a few characters but nothing overdone and it is definitely not the focal point of the story. The focal point is the society and how Citra and Rowan are trying to find a way to change it in their own way or else one might have to kill the other at the end of the apprenticeship. <br><br>There is a little bit of time needed for the set up to the story but there was also enough going on that I never lost interest. I became emotionally connected to Rowan and Citra in their very different struggles and I really enjoyed all the world details that made be question <b>if you could live forever would you really want to?</b><br><br>This will be a duology or I prefer the term duet and I was extremely shocked (like wtf just happened I didn't see that coming at all shocked) by some of the happenings going into the final quarter of the book. But I adore where the book let off for the next installment and I am really excited to see what Shusterman has planned since there seemed to be some beginnings to a few things and with NS anything can happen and you will probably find your jaw on the floor when it does.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/vp5aTn8" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480973982i/21370456.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Rating Explainantion:</b> <i>This is probably closer to a 4.25 read but I kept thinking about it days later because I love the What If of the story and I know what NS is capable of so it is a 5 star read for me.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10048581112013599827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2599932821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2599932821" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2599932821?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=best-anti-heroes">best-anti-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2599932821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11951789725746933444">UM WHAT.<br/><br/>THIS WAS SO GOOD. How did I wait so long to read it? <br/><br/>I'll post a full review at some point - but there's so many good ones out there already. For now, I'll just say that I don't normally like futuristic dystopians all that much (Marie Lu aside because she's an absolute queen) but omg I loved this one. <br/><br/>The hubs and I actually read it together on audio, and we laughed are way through it -and where shocked out of our chairs more than once.<br/><br/>Well done, Mr. Shusterman. Well done.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2483837216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483837216" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507050077p2/16201093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483837216?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=four-star">four-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=release-2017">release-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=cool-tittle">cool-tittle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483837216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4744563994360156184"><b>How dare this book mess with my fragile emotions!?!<br/><br/>I was so stressed while reading this book! UGH! This sequel is going to kill me and you are all invited to my funeral. </b><br/><br/>When I first picked up this book, I must admit, I didn't like it.<br/><br/>The premise was interesting and the writing was fine. I just didn't care for it. I read the first 90 or so pages and almost gave up. Then I decided to use one of my Audible credits and listening to the audiobook. I started it from the beginning and let myself get t</span>
  <span id="freeText4744563994360156184" style="display:none"><b>How dare this book mess with my fragile emotions!?!<br /><br />I was so stressed while reading this book! UGH! This sequel is going to kill me and you are all invited to my funeral. </b><br /><br />When I first picked up this book, I must admit, I didn't like it.<br /><br />The premise was interesting and the writing was fine. I just didn't care for it. I read the first 90 or so pages and almost gave up. Then I decided to use one of my Audible credits and listening to the audiobook. I started it from the beginning and let myself get taken in by the story. I thought I was going to be able to relax while I listened, or casually do some chores.<br /><br /><b>I was wrong!</b><br /><br />This book stressed me. I was at the edge of my seat the entire time! At one point I was washing the dishes as I listened and I honestly stood in place, holding the same plate for like ten minutes because I got so into the story!<br /><br />There were also parts that I listened to while also reading along with the book in hand and I just couldn't stop! I would tell myself that I'd only read one more chapter and before I knew it two hours of my life were gone! UGH!<br /><br />Ok, so this book is about a world where mankind no longer dies. In order to keep the population size in line, a select group of people is selected as Scythes, the only people with the authority to cause permanent death. These Scythes are trained and sent out into the world and told to kill at their discretion. Some of these Scythes are honorable, aware of the burden and necessity of their profession. Others are ruthless, disregarding the core values of the Scythedom and taking pleasure from the lives they take. Then there are our two main characters, Citra and Rowan, Scythe's apprentices who hold both the potential for goodness and darkness in their hearts.<br /><br />Through them we get to explore the interesting utopia that Shusterman has created, as well as dive into many moral debated on what it means to be human, and if we can be truly considered human now that we do not face the consequence of death. <b>Honestly, it was all fantastically written.</b> I love the idea of the Scythes, and especially that of the Thunderhead, watching over them.<br /><br /><b>So, why not the whole five stars? Well, this book actually had a lot of problems.</b><br /><br />First is the romance. <b>This book is strange in the way that romance is both a nonintrusive and yet critical part of the story.</b> This book doesn't show much romance between the two MC's, which is good. But, their supposed 'love' for each other is one of their main motivators, which is bad. <b>Having a romance that is both lacking and integral to the plot, just doesn't work.</b><br /><b>Also, there were points in the book that were there only as conflict for the sake of conflict.</b> One of the main plot points is that Citra and Rowan are set up against each other for the position of Scythe, then the stakes are raised to say that the loser will die. And this is done for no reason. It makes no sense that one should die, and they even point it out! All of this could have been avoided!<br /><br /><b>Lastly, this book is actually kind of slow</b>. Had I not listened to the audiobook, I don't think I would have enjoyed it as much. Once the plot gets going, it's actually really interesting, but it does take it a minute to really start. So, keep that in mind if you want to read this.<br /><br /><b>In the end, do I recommend this? Heck yeah! </b>I really enjoyed it and can't wait to read the sequel, Thunderhead, next month. If the cons I described aren't things that would bother you, then I definitely think you should add this to your TBR. Also, I highly recommend this as an audiobook. Trust me, it was awesome and it won't disappoint!<br /><br /><br />Follow Me Here Too:<b> <a href="http://www.thebookcovergirls.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/covergirlreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/book-cover-girl-19339391" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin'</a> || <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookcovergirls//" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://thebookcovergirls.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thebookcovergirls/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4744563994360156184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2310862579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2310862579" />
    <a title="Yusra  ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67405281-yusra"><img alt="Yusra  ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521992247p2/67405281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2310862579?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yusra  ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yusra  ✨" href="/user/show/67405281-yusra">Yusra  ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67405281-yusra?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67405281-yusra?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67405281-yusra?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67405281-yusra?shelf=fav-characters">fav-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67405281-yusra?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67405281-yusra?shelf=killing-cliffhanger">killing-cliffhanger</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2310862579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8786687192812433613"><a href='https://ibb.co/fwXDBx' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525046935i/25454864._SX540_.jpg' alt='55783_C74_EC28_4_FB9_ADE1_6_A76_D20_F1_AF1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>you can read this review and more on <a href='http://themysticmango.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog!</a><br/><br/><b> Scythe was insane. </b> I don’t think I’ve ever read something so dark and brutal and strangely addictive (that may just be because I don’t read horror). So if you’re like me and not a fan of horror movies/books, rest assured that this is definitely on the milder side.<br/><br/>That doesn’t mean it won’t be great for fans of the genre; it definitely has the entice and thrill.<br/><br/>I’ve been at a weird position practically since the start of 2018 where dystopians are</span>
  <span id="freeText8786687192812433613" style="display:none"><a href="https://ibb.co/fwXDBx" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525046935i/25454864._SX540_.jpg" alt="55783_C74_EC28_4_FB9_ADE1_6_A76_D20_F1_AF1" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>you can read this review and more on <a href="http://themysticmango.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog!</a><br><br><b> Scythe was insane. </b> I don’t think I’ve ever read something so dark and brutal and strangely addictive (that may just be because I don’t read horror). So if you’re like me and not a fan of horror movies/books, rest assured that this is definitely on the milder side.<br><br>That doesn’t mean it won’t be great for fans of the genre; it definitely has the entice and thrill.<br><br>I’ve been at a weird position practically since the start of 2018 where dystopians are so not me anymore. It was actually Lauren Oliver’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11614718.Delirium__Delirium___1_" title="Delirium (Delirium, #1) by Lauren Oliver" rel="nofollow noopener">Delirium</a> that made me rethink the genre completely and wonder if it was finally too unbelievable and cliche. But Scythe breaks all the stereotypes, crafting a dystopian world that will surely have you questioning the meanings of life and death.<br><br>On that note, I have to talk about <b> worldbuilding </b>. Especially when it comes to dystopian novels, the setting sets the entire story on a direction; whether that be good or bad, it’s up to the author. Let me tell you, (I’m going to sound like a grade school english teacher, but) I WAS VISUALIZING. I also feel like every reader will see this world unfold in a different way because of the way details are given; it’s entirely up to you, as the reader, to make this world what it is.<br><br>Scythe travels to a futuristic world where humans have completely eliminated mortality – one can live for thousands upon thousands of years. Disease, injuries, any situation that would in modern-day kill in seconds can be fixed in a maximum period of two days at revival centres.<br><br>But the population must be controlled.<br><br>For that, there are scythes. Once you are gleaned, there is no revival. There is no mercy at the hands of scythes; if you are chosen, you will be gleaned. Your family shall be granted immunity for a year.<br><br>Although the population control system reminded me of the Purge, I otherwise found that this premise was stellar, interesting and original. I was hooked from the first pages and didn’t want to let go of the world of terrible… and worse.<br><br>In this book, we follow the lives of two scythe apprentices, Citra and Rowan, training under Scythe Faraday (spoiler – I love him). They must learn to leave their compassion behind and forget their lives in order to complete training in weaponry, poisoning and other methods of gleaning.<br><br>IT WAS SO INTERESTING. I REPEAT ; IT WAS SO INSANELY GOOD.<br><br>Plot twists galore, intrigue galore, buildup galore; this was literal perfection. I’m #TeamCitra all the way, but Rowan is still adorbssss. and although romance isn’t necessary… it was preetttyyy cute, not gonna lie.<br><br>You know, I think Shusterman is a genius. Every tiny detail is paid attention to, the writing flows in the most wonderful way, he says some serious truths (u betcha, ur gonna be questioning morality and mortality like nothing before). The Thunderhead is something I am itching to know more about and it’s the name ! of ! book ! 2 ! it’s like this series was made for me, knowing what I wanted and what will make me scream in suspense.<br><br>Lastly; THE GLEANING JOURNALS. In my opinion, the highlight of this book were the various scythe journals. One of the ten commandments for scythes is they are required to keep a daily journal and boy, were they something. So many things I wanted to highlight and jot down, I could have a whole 10 page essay filled with them. At first I thought we’d have just one journal in the perspective of one scythe, but the subtle change in tone confirmed it wasn’t Curie when it came to Goddard’s first journal. It just got better and better.<br><br>also Faraday. I love you. marry me please. I LOVE HIM SO MUCH <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ can we talk about that I love you though  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>asdshfdf not even joking the ending had / has me shook right now. I need book 2 right nowwww</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8786687192812433613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3463647401" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14992427930445296172">I listened to this on audiobook over the course of months and this is, without a doubt, the BEST BOOK I have read so far this year. I am SO MAD AT MYSELF that I didn’t read it sooner. <br/><br/>Between the odd world where so much of what we know today has vanished and changed, the characters who fight so hard to prevent becoming the things they despise despite the maddening desire to do so, and how much this story had my stomach dropping, my breath catching, my eyes widening, and my whole body quite liter</span>
  <span id="freeText14992427930445296172" style="display:none">I listened to this on audiobook over the course of months and this is, without a doubt, the BEST BOOK I have read so far this year. I am SO MAD AT MYSELF that I didn’t read it sooner. <br /><br />Between the odd world where so much of what we know today has vanished and changed, the characters who fight so hard to prevent becoming the things they despise despite the maddening desire to do so, and how much this story had my stomach dropping, my breath catching, my eyes widening, and my whole body quite literally flailing around my room when shit hit the fan MANY MANY TIMES...there’s not much more to say other than I’m starting book two immediately.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IP/2Y5OmscQRwCbUFxBL8Xw4exsdDz8iCgvLC2w4wpa3SKBwzsd+tBm+rgtWHLHcmTd+EM0Xg81V7iNYZf2K2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bt1toNnbWIh72TrD4x+RGFQqc4i/3bAdupghIVO8X/D5ajuzhLqX+HOnshyiE2s1sSV2g2/FDPLlfclyWnkXvw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer17547851422870822659">Award-winning author Neal Shusterman grew up in Brooklyn, New York, where he began writing at an early age. After spending his junior and senior years of high school at the American School of Mexico City, Neal went on to UC Irvine, where he made his mark on the UCI swim team, and wrote a successful humor column. Within a year of graduating, he had his first book deal, and was hired to write a movi</span>
  <span id="freeText17547851422870822659" style="display:none">Award-winning author Neal Shusterman grew up in Brooklyn, New York, where he began writing at an early age. After spending his junior and senior years of high school at the American School of Mexico City, Neal went on to UC Irvine, where he made his mark on the UCI swim team, and wrote a successful humor column. Within a year of graduating, he had his first book deal, and was hired to write a movie script.<br /><br />In the years since, Neal has made his mark as a successful novelist, screenwriter, and television writer. As a full-time writer, he claims to be his own hardest task-master, always at work creating new stories to tell. His books have received many awards from organizations such as the International Reading Association, and the American Library Association, as well as garnering a myriad of state and local awards across the country. Neal's talents range from film directing (two short films he directed won him the coveted CINE Golden Eagle Awards) to writing music and stage plays – including book and lyrical contributions to “American Twistory,” which is currently playing in Boston. He has even tried his hand at creating Games, having developed three successful "How to Host a Mystery" game for teens, as well as seven "How to Host a Murder" games.<br /><br />As a screen and TV writer, Neal has written for the "Goosebumps" and “Animorphs” TV series, and wrote the Disney Channel Original Movie “Pixel Perfect”. Currently Neal is adapting his novel Everlost as a feature film for Universal Studios.<br /><br />Wherever Neal goes, he quickly earns a reputation as a storyteller and dynamic speaker. Much of his fiction is traceable back to stories he tells to large audiences of children and teenagers -- such as his novel The Eyes of Kid Midas. As a speaker, Neal is in constant demand at schools and conferences. Degrees in both psychology and drama give Neal a unique approach to writing. Neal's novels always deal with topics that appeal to adults as well as teens, weaving true-to-life characters into sensitive and riveting issues, and binding it all together with a unique and entertaining sense of humor.<br /><br />Of Everlost, School Library Journal wrote: “Shusterman has reimagined what happens after death and questions power and the meaning of charity. While all this is going on, he has also managed to write a rip-roaring adventure…”<br /><br />Of What Daddy Did, Voice of Youth Advocates wrote; "This is a compelling, spell-binding story... A stunning novel, impossible to put down once begun.<br /><br />Of The Schwa Was Here, School Library Journal wrote: “Shusterman's characters–reminiscent of those crafted by E. L. Konigsburg and Jerry Spinelli–are infused with the kind of controlled, precocious improbability that magically vivifies the finest children's classics.<br /><br />Of Scorpion Shards, Publisher's Weekly wrote: "Shusterman takes an outlandish comic-book concept, and, through the sheer audacity and breadth of his imagination makes it stunningly believable. A spellbinder."<br /><br />And of The Eyes of Kid Midas, The Midwest Book Review wrote "This wins our vote as one of the best young-adult titles of the year" and was called "Inspired and hypnotically readable" by School Library Journal.<br /><br />Neal Shusterman lives in Southern California with his children Brendan, Jarrod, Joelle, and Erin, who are a constant source of inspiration!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17547851422870822659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
